< review>
Unfortunately I stopped into Stir Fry to get a quick bite to eat and experienced some of the worst Chinese food I have ever had.

I chose the "Combination B" option, picking the spare ribs & sweet and sour chicken with rice, and I grabbed one Pot Sticker for good measure. The rice portion was small, especially for the amount of meat that was given, but I didn't feel the need to complain until I actually tasted the meal.

Everything was room temperature, except the pot stickers which was actually cold on the inside. Both entree meats were soggy / not crisp despite both being fried. It was the equivalent of buffet food that had sat too long under heat lamps.

I felt that I wasted $10, and I would have honestly remained hungry until I got off work. Do yourself a favor if you're looking to get a decent meal at all, just avoid Stir Fry.<//review>

<username>LULU . LIVE</username><Time>1616302943015</Time><Rating>5</Rating>< Review>
I love this small and cute wine tasting room in beautiful seaport village. It never goes wrong to end your seaport Village visit with a lovely wine tasting. I love they curate the wines from unique and delicious local wineries. The wine flight I chose is called All Star San Diego, it includes one while one rose and one red. White is Chardonnay which is very light and fresh. The rose is very special, I will say it's more like a fruity & floral type to me, kind of medium body. And my favorite is the 2015 Cab, it is bold, dry and long lasting. Cute spot and I'll go back for sure and hopefully with my friends together.</Review>

<Rating>4< /Rating><gmap_id>0x80dc01ac0f4508d5:0x2897a1e939073dd1<//gmap_id>< text>
First time here with my fiancee' and her sorority sister. The girls wanted to check out a wine spot and this was the closest one that they had from Eddie V's.

A small little quaint tasting room but with a nice patio view of the harbor. Very friendly and knowledgeable service For $20 you get 5 tastings and you get to keep the nice wine glass.

my pallet is more on the tart side. Their whites are okay but the fruit wines are a must try; especially their habanero fruit infused wine double award winner. When in the area i would definitely remember to come back and buy a bottle.</text>

< review>
Location, location, location.  We were walking/enjoying the sights on Seaport Village with no particular plan or destination.  We were looking around for a good place for a pint, when we spied the San Pasqual Winery.  It has several small tables on it's deck with a fabulous view of the yachts in doc.  The young man behind the counter was personable and knowledgable. He suggested several items and we ended-up spending over an hour sipping wine and watching the world go by.  If your looking to relax and drink a wide variety of wine in Seaport Village, this is the place!< /review>

First of all, Anatoly was very helpful in showing us around and answering all our questions. < Text>
This restaurant is located in an area where you least expected; in fact it looks like it was a former bar. The owners are pretty hands on when it comes to service and making the food (which was also a problem because the husband was the only one in the dining room and the wife was working the kitchen by herself).

They do have lot of great food here, but there are some you can skip. The beef noodle rolls is one you can skip. The Shanghai dumpling was good, and will satisfy your craving if you can't make it to SF. The fresh noodles soup was truly fresh, you can taste it from the texture and the soup base had MSG. Their small appetizer plates was a bit on the saltier side, but their tea egg was pretty flavorful. Pot stickers was a bit greasy and the taste and it didn't appear freshly made. Their green onion pancake had very minimum green onion so you don't get that taste.

Menu is also a bit confusing as their numbering  is duplicated elsewhere in the menu so make sure you point to what you want instead of calling out the number.

Although the service here was friendly the speed of food delivery was very painfully slow.. we got here at 8:00PM and didn't finish our meal until after 9:30PM< /Text>

<Review>Last week I took a date to this restaurant, and oh, what a wondrous time it was!

Reservations had been difficult to get - I had called several times the previous week, and finally got a corner table for two, in the most romantic part of the dining hall. The maitre d' eyed us to ensure our correct adherence to the strict dress code. I thought he was a bit snooty, but I could scarcely blame his probing eye. It was a Wednesday night, after all. After inspection, we were taken to our table, positioned closely to the marvelous architectural design of the service counter, a marvel to be sure. A betuxedo'd man played a soothing number on a violin as he slowly wandered the dining hall, playing at just the right volume to allow for quiet conversation, smiling and winking at each charmed couple. The couple next to us were gazing starry-eyed at each other as they fed each other french fries, and the lighting was just low enough to have the right feeling. It was destined to be a magical night under the golden arches.

Our waiter was a kindly old gentleman who brought us a delightful smile with his recommendations. "The Filet O'Fish," he said, was ‚Äúespecially fresh today and a superb choice with a glass of fine Coca Cola." I admit, I was taken by the description of crispiness, and my date was rather impressed as well. I was happy to hear that there would be no corking fee for the Coca Cola, although I kept this exuberance quiet so as not to look miserly to my date.

I had two of the Filet O' Fish sandwiches, while my date had the Quarter Pounder with Cheese. She looked radiant, the sequins in her black dress sparkling in the dimmed light, outmatched only by the glint of hunger for her delicious sandwich and, I hoped, for my overpowering masculinity. The barest drip of ketchup splashed onto the wrapper in front of her, and we laughed nervously with each other over the near fashion disaster that had posed to her dress.

After the satisfying meal, our waiter returned, suggesting a hot apple pie for dessert. I'm glad I made the splurge for this treat, these two hand-held, self-contained, apple-y goo bars. I still shake my head at the wonder of it all. By the time we had finished the pies, and were licking each other's fingers sensually for the trace flecks of cinnamon and sugar we had left behind, my date was looking at me with doe eyes. I had surely impressed her with the gourmet meal and the atmosphere.

After dinner, we slow-danced on the floor of the playground, surrounded by candles placed in recycled, decorated Big Mac boxes. It's very important to me that a company take my environmental concerns seriously, and I was glad to see this artistic display. Over the shoulder of my sweetheart, a statue of St. Ronald McDonald gazed upon me approvingly, and I winked at him in thanks. I owed the tremendous success of the date that night to his efforts in creating a wonderful setting with quality food.

I had the McLoving of a lifetime that night, and I owe it all to the fine quality of this McDonald's restaurant. It truly was a McMagical night.<//Review><Pictures>None</Pictures>< resp>
None<//resp>
